width="31" height="25" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/PR_secondary_149.svg/47px-PR_secondary_149.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/PR_secondary_149.svg/62px-PR_secondary_149.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <span typeof="mw:File"><a //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Ellipse_sign_144.svg/62px-Ellipse_sign_144.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="600" /></a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Ciales</b> (<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1177148991">.mw-parser-output .IPA-label-small{font-size:85%}.mw-parser-output .references .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .infobox .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .navbox .IPA-label-small{font-size:100%}</style><span class="IPA-label IPA-label-small">Spanish pronunciation:</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="es-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">&#91;\xcb\x88sjales&#93;</a></span>, <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1177148991"><span class="IPA-label IPA-label-small">locally</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="es-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">&#91;\xcb\x88sjale\xca\x94&#93;</a></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/Ciales_barrio-pueblo" title="Ciales barrio-pueblo">town</a> and <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Municipalities of Puerto Rico">municipality</a> of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, located on the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Central_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Cordillera Central (Puerto Rico)">Central Mountain Range</a>, northwest of <a href="/wiki/Orocovis,_Puerto_Rico" title="Orocovis, Puerto Rico">Orocovis</a>; south of <a href="/wiki/Florida,_Puerto_Rico" title="Florida, Puerto Rico">Florida</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manat%C3%AD,_Puerto_Rico" title="Manat\xc3\xad, Puerto Rico">Manat\xc3\xad</a>; east of <a href="/wiki/Utuado,_Puerto_Rico" title="Utuado, Puerto Rico">Utuado</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jayuya,_Puerto_Rico" title="Jayuya, Puerto Rico">Jayuya</a>; and west of <a href="/wiki/Morovis,_Puerto_Rico" title="Morovis, Puerto Rico">Morovis</a>. Ciales is spread over eight barrios and <a href="/wiki/Ciales_barrio-pueblo" title="Ciales barrio-pueblo">Ciales Pueblo</a> (the downtown area and the administrative center of the city). It is part of the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan-Caguas-Guaynabo_Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="San Juan-Caguas-Guaynabo Metropolitan Statistical Area">San Juan-Caguas-Guaynabo Metropolitan Statistical Area</a>.\n</p>\n<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Toponym">Toponym</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ciales,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Toponym"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Sources diverge on the origin of the Ciales name. Nineteenth-century historian <a href="/wiki/Cayetano_Coll_y_Toste" title="Cayetano Coll y Toste">Cayetano Coll y Toste</a> stated that it was named as such by then-governor Gonzalo de Ar\xc3\xb3stegui Herrera in honor of <a href="/wiki/Luis_de_Lacy" title="Luis de Lacy">General Luis de Lacy</a>, who had gone against <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_VII_of_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Ferdinand VII of Spain">Ferdinand VII\'s</a> absolutist wishes.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Coll y Toste suggested that the Villa Lacy<sup id="cite_ref-Nuestro_PR_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nuestro_PR-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> name came from the anagram "es-la-cy" anagram.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:1_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Other sources, such as Manuel \xc3\x81lvarez Nazario and Luis Hern\xc3\xa1ndez Aquino, put forward the theory that it comes from the plural of <i>cibales</i>, plural form of <i>ciba</i>, meaning "stony place" or "place of stones" in <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_language" title="Ta\xc3\xadno language">Ta\xc3\xadno</a>, which "had undergone loss of the intervocalic -b- and the addition of the Spanish suffix referring to place -al." Lisa Cathleen Green-Douglass, who carried out a study of toponymics in Puerto Rico and compared both theories, believed the latter to be most plausible since Coll y Toste, per Green-Douglass, must have defined an anagram as a reversal of syllables and the resulting "Cial" or "Cyal" would have to then be made plural.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Yet others believe it originates from the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> <i>sillar</i> (meaning "carved stones") in reference to the stones carved by the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Grande_de_Manat%C3%AD" title="R\xc3\xado Grande de Manat\xc3\xad">R\xc3\xado Grande de Manat\xc3\xad\'s</a> currents.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ciales,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Manat%C3%AD_Bridge_at_Mata_de_Pl%C3%A1tano_in_Ciales,_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Manat%C3%AD_Bridge_at_Mata_de_Pl%C3%A1tano_in_Ciales%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/220px-Manat%C3%AD_Bridge_at_Mata_de_Pl%C3%A1tano_in_Ciales%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Manat%C3%AD_Bridge_at_Mata_de_Pl%C3%A1tano_in_Ciales%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/330px-Manat%C3%AD_Bridge_at_Mata_de_Pl%C3%A1tano_in_Ciales%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Manat%C3%AD_Bridge_at_Mata_de_Pl%C3%A1tano_in_Ciales%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/440px-Manat%C3%AD_Bridge_at_Mata_de_Pl%C3%A1tano_in_Ciales%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a><figcaption> <a href="/wiki/Manat%C3%AD_Bridge_at_Mata_de_Pl%C3%A1tano" title="Manat\xc3\xad Bridge at Mata de Pl\xc3\xa1tano">Manat\xc3\xad Bridge at Mata de Pl\xc3\xa1tano</a>, in Ciales</figcaption></figure> \n<p>Until its founding on June 24, 1820, by Isidro Rodr\xc3\xadguez,<sup id="cite_ref-Nuestro_PR_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nuestro_PR-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> it was part of  the neighboring Manat\xc3\xad municipality, a process that took four years to achieve.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>On 13 August 1898, after the armistice ending the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War">Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War</a> was signed, Ciales was one of three towns that held uprisings. Led by Ventura Casellas, between three hundred and four hundred individuals proclaimed the Republic of Puerto Rico. However, it has not been determined without a shadow of a doubt whether it was a clear <a href="/wiki/Independence_movement_in_Puerto_Rico" title="Independence movement in Puerto Rico">independence-supporting event</a> or a defense of <a href="/wiki/Captaincy_General_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Captaincy General of Puerto Rico">Spanish rule</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Edwin Karli Padilla Aponte calls it an "alleged revolutionary uprising" since he finds no official historical record for it, even though it appears in a vignette in the <i>Pueblos Hispanos</i> monthly written by a Gabriel Aracelis, a possible pseudonym for <a href="/wiki/Juan_Antonio_Corretjer" title="Juan Antonio Corretjer">Juan Antonio Corretjer</a>. The column describes the battle, mentions the participants by name and connects it to the <a href="/wiki/Grito_de_Lares" title="Grito de Lares">Grito de Lares</a> by identifying a Pedro Gonz\xc3\xa1lez as a grandson of a Manuel Gonz\xc3\xa1lez who allegedly fought in the 1868 revolt, establishing a continuity between both events. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Paul_G._Miller&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Paul G. Miller (page does not exist)">Paul G. Miller</a>, <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_Education_of_Puerto_Rico#Education_Commissioners" title="Secretary of Education of Puerto Rico">Education Commissioner</a> between 1915 and 1921, considered this to be caused by the Seditious Parties (<i>Partidas Sediciosas</i>), gangs of bandits that raided Spaniards\' homes in the late-nineteenth century, an idea that Corretjer refuted.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Puerto Rico was ceded by <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> in the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War">Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War</a> under the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_of_1898" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Paris of 1898">Treaty of Paris of 1898</a> and became a territory of the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. In 1899, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_War" title="United States Department of War">United States Department of War</a> conducted a <a href="/wiki/Census" title="Census">census</a> of Puerto Rico finding that the population of Ciales was 18,115.<sup id="cite_ref-OfficeSanger1900_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OfficeSanger1900-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The first <a href="/wiki/Truss_bridge" title="Truss bridge">truss bridge</a> erected in Puerto Rico, after the signing of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1898)" title="Treaty of Paris (1898)">Treaty of Paris</a>, is in Ciales. It is over the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Grande_de_Manat%C3%AD" title="R\xc3\xado Grande de Manat\xc3\xad">R\xc3\xado Grande de Manat\xc3\xad</a> and is on the list of <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places_listings_in_Puerto_Rico" title="National Register of Historic Places listings in Puerto Rico">National Register of Historic Places</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a> struck Puerto Rico on September 20, 2017, its <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">eye</a> passing through northeastern Ciales,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> leaving all municipalities without power for months. Ciales received 19.23 inches of rain which caused landslides. An estimated 3,000 homes in Ciales were completely destroyed by Hurricane Mar\xc3\xada.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Three months after the hurricane struck, engineers were hoping to have electrical service established, at least for the Ciales barrio-pueblo (downtown) area.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The following December, the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Emergency_Management_Agency" title="Federal Emergency Management Agency">Federal Emergency Management Agency</a> announced the opening of a disaster recovery center in Ciales to attend the home and business owners, as well as tenants, affected by the hurricane.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px; height: 150px;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_landslides_in_Puerto_Rico_-_Hurricane_Maria_2017.jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="Map of landslides"><img alt="Map of landslides" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Map_of_landslides_in_Puerto_Rico_-_Hurricane_Maria_2017.jpg/120px-Map_of_landslides_in_Puerto_Rico_-_Hurricane_Maria_2017.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="89" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Map_of_landslides_in_Puerto_Rico_-_Hurricane_Maria_2017.jpg/180px-Map_of_landslides_in_Puerto_Rico_-_Hurricane_Maria_2017.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Map_of_landslides_in_Puerto_Rico_-_Hurricane_Maria_2017.jpg/240px-Map_of_landslides_in_Puerto_Rico_-_Hurricane_Maria_2017.jpg 2x" data-file-width="770" data-file-height="569" /></a></span></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">Map of landslides</div>\n\t\t</li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px; height: 150px;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:New_York_National_Guard_(37608228266).jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="National Guard of NY in Ciales after Hurricane Maria"><img alt="National Guard of NY in Ciales after Hurricane Maria" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/New_York_National_Guard_%2837608228266%29.jpg/120px-New_York_National_Guard_%2837608228266%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="90" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/New_York_National_Guard_%2837608228266%29.jpg/180px-New_York_National_Guard_%2837608228266%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/New_York_National_Guard_%2837608228266%29.jpg/240px-New_York_National_Guard_%2837608228266%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="720" /></a></span></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">National Guard of NY in Ciales after Hurricane Maria</div>\n\t\t</li>\n</ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Energy_consortium">Energy consortium</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ciales,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Energy consortium"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>An Energy Consortium was signed in late February, 2019 by <a href="/wiki/Villalba,_Puerto_Rico" title="Villalba, Puerto Rico">Villalba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orocovis" class="mw-redirect" title="Orocovis">Orocovis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Morovis" class="mw-redirect" title="Morovis">Morovis</a>, Ciales and <a href="/wiki/Barranquitas" class="mw-redirect" title="Barranquitas">Barranquitas</a> municipalities. The consortium is the first of its kind for the island. It is intended to have municipalities work together to safeguard and create resilient, and efficient energy networks, with backups for their communities. This is part of the hurricane preparedness plan of these municipalities, which were hit particularly hard by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a> on September 20, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Geography">Geography</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ciales,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Geography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Homes_and_mountainside_in_Ciales,_Puerto_Rico.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Homes_and_mountainside_in_Ciales%2C_Puerto_Rico.JPG/220px-Homes_and_mountainside_in_Ciales%2C_Puerto_Rico.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Homes_and_mountainside_in_Ciales%2C_Puerto_Rico.JPG/330px-Homes_and_mountainside_in_Ciales%2C_Puerto_Rico.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Homes_and_mountainside_in_Ciales%2C_Puerto_Rico.JPG/440px-Homes_and_mountainside_in_Ciales%2C_Puerto_Rico.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a><figcaption>View of homes and mountainside of an area of Ciales from <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Paseo Lineal Juan Antonio Corretjera</i></span> lookout point</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The northern part of the municipality is located in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Karst_(Puerto_Rico)" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Karst (Puerto Rico)">Northern Karst</a> zone of Puerto Rico while the southern part is in the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Central_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Cordillera Central (Puerto Rico)">Cordillera Central</a>. The highest point in the municipality is <a href="/wiki/Cerro_Rosa" title="Cerro Rosa">Cerro Rosa</a> at 4,143 feet (1,262&#160;m), itself the third highest point in Puerto Rico. Ciales is home to a forest reserve called <a href="/wiki/Toro_Negro_State_Forest" title="Toro Negro State Forest">Toro Negro Forest Reserve</a> and a number of rivers including: <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Cialitos" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Cialitos">R\xc3\xado Cialitos</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Grande_de_Manat%C3%AD" title="R\xc3\xado Grande de Manat\xc3\xad">R\xc3\xado Grande de Manat\xc3\xad</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Toro_Negro" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Toro Negro">R\xc3\xado Toro Negro</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Yunes" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Yunes">R\xc3\xado Yunes</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Pozas, and Barbas.<sup id="cite_ref-flyer_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flyer-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Over 40% of its territory falls within protected areas, ranking as the 6th municipality with the largest portion of protected territory overall.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Consequentially, the destruction of 508 native planted trees at the Finca Don Ingenio in the Toro Negro Forest Reserve in August 2021 was caused for an uproar. The trees, which included <a href="/wiki/Ceiba" title="Ceiba">ceiba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thespesia_grandiflora" title="Thespesia grandiflora">maga</a> specimens, had been planted as part of the <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Mar\xc3\xada</a> recovery by the Puerto Rico Conservation Trust\'s <i>Para La Naturaleza</i> program.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>As part of the karst region, there are many caves, such as Archillas Cave, located in <a href="/wiki/Jaguas,_Ciales,_Puerto_Rico" title="Jaguas, Ciales, Puerto Rico">Jaguas Ventana</a>, named after the family that owns it. Since Ciales has a saying "to graduate as a Ciale\xc3\xb1o, you have to go up to the Archillas,"<sup id="cite_ref-Romanization_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Romanization-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>a<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> then-mayor <a href="/wiki/Luis_Maldonado_(politician)" title="Luis Maldonado (politician)">Luis R. Maldonado Rodriguez</a> attempted to acquire it. The cave has been associated with the Arcaicos, though it also holds some <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Ta\xc3\xadno">Ta\xc3\xadno</a> petroglyphs. The cave system was first studied by <a href="/wiki/Alphonse_Pinart" title="Alphonse Pinart">Alphonse L. Pinart</a> in 1890. Since then several investigations have been carried out that have aided in the identification of <a href="/wiki/Silex" title="Silex">silex</a> as the main material used by the Ta\xc3\xadno for their carving tools and the discovery of <a href="/wiki/Taino_archaeology" class="mw-redirect" title="Taino archaeology">ceramic fragments</a>, as well as the theory that the caves were used for rituals, such as <a href="/wiki/Cohoba" title="Cohoba">cojoba-induced ceremonies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> During his research in the early 1900s, <a href="/wiki/Jesse_Walter_Fewkes" title="Jesse Walter Fewkes">Jesse Walter Fewkes</a> identified the Ciales\' caves as some those occupied by the Ta\xc3\xadno<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> as well as several of the best preserved sites with <a href="/wiki/Taino_archaeology" class="mw-redirect" title="Taino archaeology">their stone-carved implements</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> One of these caves, <i>La Cohoba</i> Cave, was named after the namesake object found in it.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Another notable find, carried out by Carlos M. Ayes Su\xc3\xa1rez, was of a zoomorphic idol from the Arcaico era in <a href="/wiki/Pesas,_Ciales,_Puerto_Rico" title="Pesas, Ciales, Puerto Rico">Pesas</a> that "consists of a <a href="/wiki/Hammerstone" title="Hammerstone">cobble</a> that presents an engraved representation seemingly zoomorphic in shape" which is considered unique in Puerto Rico and the Antilles.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Due to the mountainous nature of Ciales\' topography, landslides occur, such as the rock fall that occurred in June 2021 in <a href="/wiki/Pozas,_Ciales,_Puerto_Rico" title="Pozas, Ciales, Puerto Rico">Pozas</a> that caused several buildings and fences to be destroyed, road closures and the removal of residents.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Barrios">Barrios</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ciales,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Barrios"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ciales,_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Ciales%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png/220px-Ciales%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="238" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Ciales%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png/330px-Ciales%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Ciales%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png/440px-Ciales%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png 2x" data-file-width="1100" data-file-height="1191" /></a><figcaption>Ciales map with barrio subdivisions</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Like all municipalities of Puerto Rico, Ciales is subdivided into <a href="/wiki/Barrios_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Barrios of Puerto Rico">barrios</a>. The municipal buildings, central square and large Catholic church are located in a barrio referred to as <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">"el pueblo"</i></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-Pico_1969_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pico_1969-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Law2015_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law2015-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-US2010Census_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US2010Census-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1184024115">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .div-col-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output .div-col dd{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style><div class="div-col" style="column-width: 15em;">\n<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Ciales_barrio-pueblo" title="Ciales mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sectors">Sectors</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ciales,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Sectors"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1236090951">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_barrios_and_sectors_of_Ciales,_Puerto_Rico" title="List of barrios and sectors of Ciales, Puerto Rico">List of barrios and sectors of Ciales, Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<p>Barrios (which are like <a href="/wiki/Minor_civil_divisions" class="mw-redirect" title="Minor civil divisions">minor civil divisions</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-Barrio-Pueblo_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barrio-Pueblo-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> are further subdivided into smaller areas called <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">sectores</i></span>  (<i>sectors</i> in English).  The types of <i>sectores</i> may vary, from <i>sector</i> to <i>urbanizaci\xc3\xb3n</i> to <i>reparto</i> to <i>barriada</i> to <i>residencial</i>, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Special_Communities">Special Communities</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ciales,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Special Communities"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Office_for_Socioeconomic_and_Community_Development" title="Puerto Rico Office for Socioeconomic and Community Development">Puerto Rico Office for Socioeconomic and Community Development</a></div>\n<p><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Comunidades Especiales de Puerto Rico</i></span> (Special Communities of Puerto Rico) are marginalized communities whose citizens are experiencing a certain amount of <a href="/wiki/Social_exclusion" title="Social exclusion">social exclusion</a>. A map shows these communities occur in nearly every municipality of the commonwealth. Of the 742 places that were on the list in 2014, the following barrios, communities, sectors, or neighborhoods were in Ciales: Sector El Hoyo in Pozas, Calle Morovis, Comunidad Los Ortega, Cruces-Cialitos, Parcelas Cordillera, Parcelas Mar\xc3\xada, Parcelas Segu\xc3\xad, Santa Clara, and Toro Negro.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Demographics">Demographics</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ciales,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Demographics"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1224496135">.mw-parser-output class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<p>Ciales has one of the lowest percentages of <a href="/wiki/English_language_in_Puerto_Rico" title="English language in Puerto Rico">English speakers in Puerto Rico.</a><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>When researching the town\'s parochial baptismal records historian <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Pic%C3%B3" title="Fernando Pic\xc3\xb3">Fernando Pic\xc3\xb3</a> found that more than half the offspring baptised at the end of the nineteenth century were <a href="/wiki/Born_out_of_wedlock" class="mw-redirect" title="Born out of wedlock">born out of wedlock</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Tourism">Tourism</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ciales,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Tourism"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>To stimulate local tourism, the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Tourism_Company" title="Puerto Rico Tourism Company">Puerto Rico Tourism Company</a> launched the <i>Voy Turistiendo</i> ("I\'m Touring") campaign, with a passport book and website. The Ciales page lists <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Museo Juan Antonio Corretjer</i></span>, <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Puente Mata de Pl\xc3\xa1tano</i></span>, and <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Cascada Las Delicias</i></span>, as places of interest.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Landmarks_and_places_of_interest">Landmarks and places of interest</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ciales,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Landmarks and places of interest"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Coffee_Museum,_Ciales,_Puerto_Rico_(7).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Coffee_Museum%2C_Ciales%2C_Puerto_Rico_%287%29.jpg/140px-Coffee_Museum%2C_Ciales%2C_Puerto_Rico_%287%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="140" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Coffee_Museum%2C_Ciales%2C_Puerto_Rico_%287%29.jpg/280px-Coffee_Museum%2C_Ciales%2C_Puerto_Rico_%287%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2736" data-file-height="3648" /></a><figcaption>Coffee Museum, Ciales, Puerto Rico</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Places of interest in Ciales include:<sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Artesan\xc3\xada en Muebles La Ciale\xc3\xb1a</i></span>, family-owned factory that produces widely recognized enea grass-weaved furniture<sup id="cite_ref-:0_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Aserrado Fernando Otero</i></span>, located in <a href="/wiki/Hato_Viejo,_Ciales,_Puerto_Rico" title="Hato Viejo, Ciales, Puerto Rico">Hato Viejo</a>, it is the largest sawmill in Puerto Rico of native woods.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Hacienda Carvajal</i></span>, <a href="/wiki/Environmental_education" title="Environmental education">environmental education</a> coffee and cacao farm that also houses a printing museum and a <i><a href="/wiki/Batey_(game)" title="Batey (game)">batey</a>.</i><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Hacienda Negr\xc3\xb3n</i></span><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>Las Archillas Cave<sup id="cite_ref-:2_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>Las Golondrinas Cave</li>\n<li>Yuy\xc3\xba Cave<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>Parada Choferil</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Toro_Negro_State_Forest" title="Toro Negro State Forest">Toro Negro Forest Reserve</a></li>\n<li><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Paseo Lineal Juan Antonio Corretjer</i></span>, a lookout<sup id="cite_ref-:0_2-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Museo Biblioteca Casa Corretjer</i></span>, houses the library of <a href="/wiki/Juan_Antonio_Corretjer" title="Juan Antonio Corretjer">Juan Antonio Corretjer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_2-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Museo del Caf\xc3\xa9</i></span>, a coffee museum<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Young_people_horse-back_riding_in_Ciales,_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Young_people_horse-back_riding_in_Ciales%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/220px-Young_people_horse-back_riding_in_Ciales%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Young_people_horse-back_riding_in_Ciales%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/330px-Young_people_horse-back_riding_in_Ciales%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Young_people_horse-back_riding_in_Ciales%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/440px-Young_people_horse-back_riding_in_Ciales%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a><figcaption>Young people horse-back riding in Ciales, Puerto Rico</figcaption></figure>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Culture">Culture</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ciales,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Culture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Festivals_and_events">Festivals and events</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ciales,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Festivals and events"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Ciales celebrates its <a href="/wiki/Fiestas_patronales_in_Puerto_Rico" title="Fiestas patronales in Puerto Rico">patron saint</a> festival in October. The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Fiestas Patronales de Nuestra Se\xc3\xb1ora del Rosario y San Jose</i></span> is a religious and cultural celebration that generally features parades, games, artisans, amusement rides, regional food, and live entertainment.<sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The festival has featured live performances by well-known artists such as <a href="/wiki/Sabor_Latino" title="Sabor Latino">Sabor Latino</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Fiestas_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fiestas-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Other festivals and events celebrated in Ciales include:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Epiphany_(holiday)" title="Epiphany (holiday)">Three King\'s Day</a>, held in January</li>\n<li>Corretjer Cantata, held in March</li>\n<li>Fresh Water Festival (in <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <i lang="es">Festival de Agua Dulce</i>), <a href="/wiki/Mud_bogging" title="Mud bogging">mud bogging</a> competition and music festival held in August<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>Front\xc3\xb3n Festival, held in July</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Elijah" title="Elijah">Saint El\xc3\xadas</a> Festival, held in July</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sports">Sports</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ciales,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Sports"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Ciales is the home town of <a href="/wiki/Juan_%22Pach%C3%ADn%22_Vicens" class="mw-redirect" title="Juan &quot;Pach\xc3\xadn&quot; Vicens">Juan "Pach\xc3\xadn" Vicens</a> - Puerto Rico\'s national basketball star, named Best Player in the World at the 1959 World Basketball Championship, Santiago de Chile (a.k.a., Juan "Pach\xc3\xadn" Vicens, "Astro del Bal\xc3\xb3n", "El Jeep"; younger brother of Puerto Rico\'s National Poet, Nimia Vicens, who also hailed from Ciales). Their middle brother, <a href="/wiki/Enrique_A._Vic%C3%A9ns" class="mw-redirect" title="Enrique A. Vic\xc3\xa9ns">Enrique "Coco" Vicens</a>, a former Puerto Rico Senator, was a track and field athlete in his own right.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Economy">Economy</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ciales,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Economy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Agriculture">Agriculture</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ciales,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Agriculture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The Ciales economy has always depended heavily on agriculture, especially coffee products, minor fruits (such as lettuce) and dairy production.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_2-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Government">Government</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ciales,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Government"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mayoralty_in_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Mayoralty in Puerto Rico">Mayoralty in Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Town_Hall_in_Ciales_barrio-pueblo,_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Town_Hall_in_Ciales_barrio-pueblo%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/120px-Town_Hall_in_Ciales_barrio-pueblo%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="160" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Town_Hall_in_Ciales_barrio-pueblo%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/180px-Town_Hall_in_Ciales_barrio-pueblo%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Town_Hall_in_Ciales_barrio-pueblo%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/240px-Town_Hall_in_Ciales_barrio-pueblo%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2357" data-file-height="3143" /></a><figcaption>Town Hall in Ciales barrio-pueblo, Puerto Rico</figcaption></figure>\n<p>All municipalities in Puerto Rico are administered by a <a href="/wiki/Mayor" title="Mayor">mayor</a>, elected every four years. The current mayor of Ciales is <a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_Burgos_Otero&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Alexander Burgos Otero (page does not exist)">Alexander Burgos Otero</a>, of the <a href="/wiki/New_Progressive_Party_(Puerto_Rico)" title="New Progressive Party (Puerto Rico)">Progressive New Party</a> (PNP) who had previously served in the municipal legislature and grandson of previous Ciales mayor, Roque Otero Cort\xc3\xa9s. He was elected at the <a href="/wiki/2020_Puerto_Rican_general_election" title="2020 Puerto Rican general election">2020 general elections</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The city belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Senatorial_district_III" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rico Senatorial district III">Puerto Rico Senatorial district III</a>, which is represented by two Senators. In 2008, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Emilio_Gonz%C3%A1lez_Vel%C3%A1zquez" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Emilio Gonz\xc3\xa1lez Vel\xc3\xa1zquez">Jos\xc3\xa9 Emilio Gonz\xc3\xa1lez Vel\xc3\xa1zquez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Angel_Mart%C3%ADnez_Santiago" class="mw-redirect" title="Angel Mart\xc3\xadnez Santiago">Angel Mart\xc3\xadnez Santiago</a> were elected as District Senators.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Symbols">Symbols</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ciales,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Symbols"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">municipio</i></span> has an official flag and coat of arms.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On the 150th anniversary of the founding of Ciales, the flag and coat of arms were adopted with Resolution No. 13 Series 1969\xe2\x80\x931970, sanctioned by Don Ismael Nazario, who was mayor at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Flag">Flag</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ciales,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Flag"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The flag is divided into seven unequal stripes described in sequence: yellow, red, yellow, purple, yellow, red, and yellow.<sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Coat_of_arms">Coat of arms</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ciales,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Coat of arms"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The coat of arms consists of a gold shield with a lion standing on its rear legs and silver-plated nails grasping a silver coiled parchment between its front claws. The lion also shows a red tongue. Above the lion in the superior part of the shield are located three heraldic roses arranged horizontally with red petals and green leaves. A golden crown of three towers rests on the shield. The three towers are united by walls, simulating masonry blocks. The shield is surrounded by a crown of coffee tree branches with their berries, all in natural colors.<sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_13-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Nicknames">Nicknames</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ciales,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Nicknames"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<ul><li>Cohoba City (<a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <i lang="es">Ciudad de la cojoba</i>) for the discover of instruments used by the Ta\xc3\xadno in the <a href="/wiki/Cohoba" title="Cohoba">Cohoba ritual</a>, whereby they inhaled the hallucinogenic powder extracted from the <a href="/wiki/Cojoba" title="Cojoba">cojoba</a> seeds.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_2-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:2_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>Town of the Brave (<span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Pueblo de los valerosos</i></span>) for the high concentration of <a href="/wiki/Independence_movement_in_Puerto_Rico" title="Independence movement in Puerto Rico">independence supports</a>, such as Juan Antonio Corretjer, some of which participated in the <a href="/wiki/Grito_de_Lares" title="Grito de Lares">Grito de Lares</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_2-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>Cradle of Poets (<span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Cuna de poetas</i></span>) due to it being the birthplace of several poets, such as Juan Antonio Corretjer<sup id="cite_ref-:0_2-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and Nimia Vic\xc3\xa9ns,<sup id="cite_ref-:3_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> both considered Puerto Rico\'s <a href="/wiki/National_poet" title="National poet">national poets</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:4_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>Central Cordillera Gate (<span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Puerta de la Cordillera Central</i></span>) owing to its geographic location on the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Central_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Cordillera Central (Puerto Rico)">Cordillera Central</a> mountainous range.<sup id="cite_ref-flyer_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flyer-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>Switzerland of Puerto Rico (<span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Suiza de Puerto Rico</i></span>) on account of "its similarity to European valleys with abundant vegetation," and the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_chalet_style" title="Swiss chalet style">wooden houses</a> that are located in them.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Transportation">Transportation</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ciales,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Transportation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ciales,_Puerto_Rico_Terminal_for_public_transportation.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Ciales%2C_Puerto_Rico_Terminal_for_public_transportation.jpg/120px-Ciales%2C_Puerto_Rico_Terminal_for_public_transportation.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="103" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Ciales%2C_Puerto_Rico_Terminal_for_public_transportation.jpg/180px-Ciales%2C_Puerto_Rico_Terminal_for_public_transportation.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Ciales%2C_Puerto_Rico_Terminal_for_public_transportation.jpg/240px-Ciales%2C_Puerto_Rico_Terminal_for_public_transportation.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3174" data-file-height="2726" /></a><figcaption><i>Terminal de Carros P\xc3\xbablicos Ciales</i> on <i>Calle Palmer</i></figcaption></figure><p>There is a public transportation terminal in <a href="/wiki/Ciales_barrio-pueblo" title="Ciales barrio-pueblo">downtown Ciales</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In addition, there are 18 bridges in Ciales,<sup id="cite_ref-bridge_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bridge-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> including the <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">NRHP</a>-listed <a href="/wiki/Manat%C3%AD_Bridge_at_Mata_de_Pl%C3%A1tano" title="Manat\xc3\xad Bridge at Mata de Pl\xc3\xa1tano">Manat\xc3\xad Bridge at Mata de Pl\xc3\xa1tano</a>.\n</p><div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Notable_people_from_Ciales">Notable people from Ciales</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ciales,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Notable people from Ciales"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<ul><li>Armando Carlo Asencio Rosado-<i><a href="/wiki/Barril_de_bomba" title="Barril de bomba">barril de bomba</a></i> artisan.<sup the <i>Los Pleneros de la Cresta</i> quintet.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span
